Player_Black (to Proxy):

I'll go with a knight maneuver that tightens the noose around White’s lone king. In this position the key observation is that White’s king on g1 has almost no escape squares—the bishop on h3 already covers f1 and g2, and with the knight on d3 controlling f2, the only remaining square is h1. 

By playing the move d3f2 (moving the knight from d3 to f2), the knight will cover h1 as well. Although the move doesn’t check immediately, it leaves White only a pawn move (from a2) for additional play while the king remains trapped. This sets up a mating net so that a precise follow‑up (for example, with the queen) will soon deliver mate.

So my move is: make_move d3f2

Player_Black (to Proxy):

The move I recommend is to move the queen from g5 to g2, which delivers checkmate. 

Let me explain briefly: After making the move Qg2, the queen sits directly on the diagonal with the white king at h1 (since h1 is exactly one diagonal step from g2), and its powerful range covers all escape squares. In this position the white king has no legal move:
 • It cannot move to g1 because the queen on g2 also covers that file.
 • It cannot capture the queen on g2 because the bishop on h3 defends that square.
 • No other white piece is available to block or capture.

Thus, Qg2 (UCI notation: g5g2) is a mate.

I'll now execute the move.

make_move g5g2
